# Problem 2881

- Domain: `coding`

## Problem

```text
Given an array of strings words and a character separator, split each string in words by separator.
Return an array of strings containing the new strings formed after the splits, excluding empty strings.
Notes

separator is used to determine where the split should occur, but it is not included as part of the resulting strings.
A split may result in more than two strings.
The resulting strings must maintain the same order as they were initially given.

 
Example 1:

Input: words = ["one.two.three","four.five","six"], separator = "."
Output: ["one","two","three","four","five","six"]
Explanation: In this example we split as follows:

"one.two.three" splits into "one", "two", "three"
"four.five" splits into "four", "five"
"six" splits into "six" 

Hence, the resulting array is ["one","two","three","four","five","six"].
Example 2:

Input: words = ["$easy$","$problem$"], separator = "$"
Output: ["easy","problem"]
Explanation: In this example we split as follows: 

"$easy$" splits into "easy" (excluding empty strings)
"$problem$" splits into "problem" (excluding empty strings)

Hence, the resulting array is ["easy","problem"].

Example 3:

Input: words = ["|||"], separator = "|"
Output: []
Explanation: In this example the resulting split of "|||" will contain only empty strings, so we return an empty array []. 
 
Constraints:

1 <= words.length <= 100
1 <= words[i].length <= 20
characters in words[i] are either lowercase English letters or characters from the string ".,|$#@" (excluding the quotes)
separator is a character from the string ".,|$#@" (excluding the quotes)
```

### Starter Code

```python
class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
```

## Generation

### System Prompt

```text
You are an expert Python programmer. You will be given a question (problem specification) and will generate a correct Python program that matches the specification and passes all tests.
```

### User Prompt

```text
### Question:
Given an array of strings words and a character separator, split each string in words by separator.
Return an array of strings containing the new strings formed after the splits, excluding empty strings.
Notes

separator is used to determine where the split should occur, but it is not included as part of the resulting strings.
A split may result in more than two strings.
The resulting strings must maintain the same order as they were initially given.

 
Example 1:

Input: words = ["one.two.three","four.five","six"], separator = "."
Output: ["one","two","three","four","five","six"]
Explanation: In this example we split as follows:

"one.two.three" splits into "one", "two", "three"
"four.five" splits into "four", "five"
"six" splits into "six" 

Hence, the resulting array is ["one","two","three","four","five","six"].
Example 2:

Input: words = ["$easy$","$problem$"], separator = "$"
Output: ["easy","problem"]
Explanation: In this example we split as follows: 

"$easy$" splits into "easy" (excluding empty strings)
"$problem$" splits into "problem" (excluding empty strings)

Hence, the resulting array is ["easy","problem"].

Example 3:

Input: words = ["|||"], separator = "|"
Output: []
Explanation: In this example the resulting split of "|||" will contain only empty strings, so we return an empty array []. 
 
Constraints:

1 <= words.length <= 100
1 <= words[i].length <= 20
characters in words[i] are either lowercase English letters or characters from the string ".,|$#@" (excluding the quotes)
separator is a character from the string ".,|$#@" (excluding the quotes)

### Format: You will use the following starter code to write the solution to the problem and enclose your code within delimiters.
```python
class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        
```

### Answer: (use the provided format with backticks)
```

### Outputs

<details>
<summary>Generation 1</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p != "":
                    result.append(p)
        return result
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 2</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p != "":
                    result.append(p)
        return result

<summary>Generation 8</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            # split and exclude empty strings
            parts = [p for p in w.split(separator) if p]
            result.extend(parts)
        return result
```
```

        result: List[str] = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p:  # exclude empty strings
                    result.append(p)
        return result

```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p:  # exclude empty strings
                    result.append(p)
        return result
```

<details>
<summary>full attempt 1</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p != "":
                    result.append(p)
        return result
```
```

<summary>full attempt 8</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            # split and exclude empty strings
            parts = [p for p in w.split(separator) if p]
            result.extend(parts)
        return result
```
```

</details>

        result: List[str] = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p:  # exclude empty strings
                    result.append(p)
        return result
```

### Baseline

### System Prompt

```text
You are an expert Python programmer. You will be given a question (problem specification) and will generate a correct Python program that matches the specification and passes all tests.
```

### User Prompt

```text
### Question:
Given an array of strings words and a character separator, split each string in words by separator.
Return an array of strings containing the new strings formed after the splits, excluding empty strings.
Notes

separator is used to determine where the split should occur, but it is not included as part of the resulting strings.
A split may result in more than two strings.
The resulting strings must maintain the same order as they were initially given.

 
Example 1:

Input: words = ["one.two.three","four.five","six"], separator = "."
Output: ["one","two","three","four","five","six"]
Explanation: In this example we split as follows:

"one.two.three" splits into "one", "two", "three"
"four.five" splits into "four", "five"
"six" splits into "six" 

Hence, the resulting array is ["one","two","three","four","five","six"].
Example 2:

Input: words = ["$easy$","$problem$"], separator = "$"
Output: ["easy","problem"]
Explanation: In this example we split as follows: 

"$easy$" splits into "easy" (excluding empty strings)
"$problem$" splits into "problem" (excluding empty strings)

Hence, the resulting array is ["easy","problem"].

Example 3:

Input: words = ["|||"], separator = "|"
Output: []
Explanation: In this example the resulting split of "|||" will contain only empty strings, so we return an empty array []. 
 
Constraints:

1 <= words.length <= 100
1 <= words[i].length <= 20
characters in words[i] are either lowercase English letters or characters from the string ".,|$#@" (excluding the quotes)
separator is a character from the string ".,|$#@" (excluding the quotes)

### Format: You will use the following starter code to write the solution to the problem and enclose your code within delimiters.
```python
class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        
```

### Answer: (use the provided format with backticks)
```

from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result: List[str] = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p != "":
                    result.append(p)
        return result
```

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result: List[str] = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p != "":
                    result.append(p)
        return result
```
```

from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        res: List[str] = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p:  # exclude empty strings
                    res.append(p)
        return res

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            # Split and exclude empty strings
            parts = w.split(separator)
            for p in parts:
                if p:  # excludes empty strings
                    result.append(p)
        return result

<summary>Augmented generation 7</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            # split and exclude empty strings
            parts = [p for p in w.split(separator) if p]
            result.extend(parts)
        return result
```
```

</details>

```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def splitWordsBySeparator(self, words: List[str], separator: str) -> List[str]:
        result = []
        for w in words:
            parts = w.split(separator)
            result.extend([p for p in parts if p])  # exclude empty strings
        return result
```
